## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the features are position x, velocity v, and time t, which matches second-order oscillator dynamics written as a first-order system dv_dt = f(x,v,t). Common models include restoring forces (linear or nonlinear), damping (linear or nonlinear), and external/parametric forcing as explicit functions of t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = -c0 * x (mass-normalized restoring acceleration)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (small-amplitude motion with fluid/viscous losses)
- Constant-force bias / gravity offset: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (equilibrium shifted by constant acceleration)
- Time-harmonic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (driven oscillator / resonance)
- Parametric stiffness modulation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametrically excited oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (stronger nonlinear restoring at larger amplitude)
- Quadratic drag (aerodynamic): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (drag dominated by speed-squared losses)
- Nonlinear damping via cubic velocity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (phenomenological nonlinear dissipation)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (limit cycle from velocity-dependent damping)
- Pendulum (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (angular oscillator with sine restoring torque)
- Nonlinear stiffness with shift: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1) - c2 * (x - c1)**3 - c3 * v (nonlinear spring about displaced equilibrium)
- Time-varying damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * v (modulated dissipation / active control)
- Mixed nonlinearities and forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v - c3 * v * Abs(v) + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (common composite fit for experimental oscillators)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force symmetry: conservative springs typically give odd functions of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x - c*x**3); even powers in x often indicate broken symmetry or shifted equilibrium (x - c).
- Energy-conserving form (no damping/forcing): dv_dt depending only on x (not on v or t) suggests a potential system where total energy 0.5*v**2 + U(x) is approximately conserved.
- Damping identification: terms proportional to v imply viscous losses; v*Abs(v) implies quadratic/aerodynamic drag; v**3 can mimic amplitude-dependent damping in structures.
- Self-excitation / limit cycles: negative damping at small amplitude captured by (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v; these typically stabilize oscillation amplitude rather than decay to rest.
- External driving vs parametric excitation: additive sin(c*t) terms indicate direct forcing; time-periodic coefficients multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x) indicate parametric excitation and can produce instability tongues.
- Geometric nonlinearity clue: sin(c*x) restoring terms are characteristic of pendulum-like kinematics; polynomial truncations (-x + x**3/6 ...) may appear if data cover modest angles.
- Hardening/softening behavior: the sign of the cubic stiffness term (-c*x**3) controls amplitude-dependent frequency shift (hardening vs softening).
- Bias/offset effects: a constant term in dv_dt or a shift (x - c) indicates an equilibrium displaced by preload, gravity component, or sensor bias.
- Velocity-position coupling beyond damping: cross terms like x*v (or x**2*v) often represent nonlinear damping or weak coupling/feedback; they are less consistent with purely conservative mechanics.

### Candidate with **log(|v|+1)** explicitly (closest on the log part)
81: \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 v|v| + c3\sin(c4\log(c5|v|+1)+c6)\).

- Could we make the sine term equal a pure \(\log(|v|+1)\)? No. A sine of a log is bounded and oscillatory in \(\log\), while \(\log(|v|+1)\) is unbounded and monotone in \(|v|\). The only way to avoid mismatch is set \(c3=0\), but then the log disappears entirely. So 81 cannot match.

20: \( \dots + c3 x^{c4}\log(c5|v|+1)\). This can create an \(x\log(|v|+1)\) coupling, but GT needs a **pure** \(\log(|v|+1)\) term (independent of \(x\)) and an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term. If set \(c4=0\), then \(x^{c4}=1\) and you can match the pure log term by choosing \(c3=-0.6247374\) and \(c5=1\). However then you still lack the required \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term (and you’ve used the only log to match the pure log). If instead keep \(x^{c4}=x\), you get \(x\log(|v|+1)\), which GT does not have. So 20 cannot match.

24: \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 e^{c3 x}\log(c4|v|+1)\). As with 244, you can set \(c3=0\) to get a constant multiplier and match the pure log term, but still no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Not match.

89: includes \(\exp(c4|v|)\log(c5|x|+1)\): wrong dependence (log in \(|x|\), not \(|v|\)). Not match.

186: log of \(|c5 e^{c6 v} + c7\cos(c8 t)|\): wrong dependence and includes \(t\). Not match.

1: has \(\sin(\cdots\log(c5 e^{c6|v|}+1)+\cdots)\): bounded oscillatory; cannot equal the needed unbounded \(\log(|v|+1)\). Not match.

### The decisive missing structure: \(x|v|^{1/3}\)
Scanning all candidates: none contains a term of the form \(x\cdot |v|^{p}\) with a free exponent \(p\) that could be set to \(1/3\). The only \(|v|^{c}\) appearance is in GT-like fashion nowhere; candidates mostly have \(v|v|\), \(v^2\), \(v^3\), \(v^{c}\) (without absolute), or logs/sines of logs. Candidate 122 has \(|v|^{c4}\) but multiplied by \(\log(|x|+1)\), not by \(x\), and also uses \(|x|\) (non-equivalent to \(x\) on a sign-changing domain). No candidate provides the required linear-in-\(x\) times fractional power of \(|v|\) term.

Because GT includes the non-removable coupling \(-3.5822062\cdot 0.0479282\; x|v|^{1/3}\), any candidate lacking an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) mechanism cannot be made identical for all real \(x,v\).

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:**
`-0.0441723*v³ - 0.333481*v*(1 - v²) - 1.24947*v - 3.58221*x*(0.047928*|v|^(1/3) + 1) - 0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.0441723*v³`
- `-0.333481*v + 0.333481*v³`
- `-1.24947*v`
- `-3.58221*x - 3.58221*0.047928*x*|v|^(1/3)`
- `-0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Combining terms:
- **v³ terms:** `-0.0441723 + 0.333481 = 0.289309` → `0.289309*v³`
- **v terms:** `-0.333481 - 1.24947 = -1.58295` → `-1.58295*v`
- **x terms:** `-3.58221*x`
- **x*|v|^(1/3) terms:** `-0.17166*x*|v|^(1/3)`
- **log term:** `-0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

So GT = `-3.58221*x + (-1.58295)*v + 0.289309*v³ - 0.17166*x*|v|^(1/3) - 0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `v` (linear)
3. `v³`
4. `x*|v|^(1/3)`
5. `log(|v| + 1)`

Now I need to check each candidate. A candidate matches only if it can express ALL five basis functions exactly. Let me focus on candidates that have enough complexity.

Most candidates are clearly missing key terms. Let me identify which candidates could potentially match by having the right structure.

The GT requires: `x`, `v`, `v³`, `x*|v|^(1/3)`, and `log(|v|+1)`. These are five linearly independent basis functions. No candidate can match unless it contains all five (or equivalent representations).

Let me scan through all candidates systematically:

- Candidates with `v³` or `v*Abs(v)` (which equals `v*|v|`, not `v³`): Note `v*|v| ≠ v³` since for negative v, `v*|v| = -v² ≠ v³ = -|v|³`. Actually wait: `v*|v| = sign(v)*v² = |v|*v`, while `v³ = v*v² = v*|v|²`. These are different.

- Candidates with `v**3`: 44, 49, 50, 68, 69, 87, 88, 102, 103, 172, 187, 202, 203, 222, 257, 263, 264, 273, 274, 279.

None of these also contain `x*|v|^(1/3)` and `log(|v|+1)`.

- Candidates with `log(...)` involving `|v|`: Candidate 20 has `x**c4*log(c5*Abs(v)+1)` and `v*Abs(v)`. Setting c4=1 gives `x*log(|v|+1)` but we need `x*|v|^(1/3)` separately.

- Candidate 81: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v*Abs(v) + c3*sin(c4*log(c5*Abs(v)+1)+c6)` — has sin of log, not the right form.

No candidate contains all five required basis functions (`x`, `v`, `v³`, `x*|v|^(1/3)`, `log(|v|+1)`).

After careful analysis of all 292 candidates, none can represent all five linearly independent basis functions present in the GT.
